## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material. Temperature typically softens materials (reducing modulus and yield stress), while strain hardening increases stress with deformation. Classical constitutive models combine these effects multiplicatively or additively.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) (linear elasticity with T-dependent modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear strain hardening, Hollomon model)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * epsilon (elastic + plastic strain contributions)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Johnson-Cook strength (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook with homologous temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T)**c4 (power-law thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturation hardening model)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * exp(c3 * T) (saturation hardening with Arrhenius-type softening)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated flow stress)
- Linear thermal softening with hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T) (multiplicative thermal effect)
- Swift model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal activation)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive law)
- Hyperbolic sine flow law: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) applied to stress
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), characteristic of Voce-type models
- Multiplicative decomposition of strain and temperature effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), separable constitutive structure
- Initial yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in stress (sigma = c0 + f(epsilon)), representing yield point
- Power-law creep behavior → sigma proportional to epsilon_dot^(1/n), or equivalently strain raised to fractional power
- Shifted power law for pre-strain → (epsilon + c0)**c1 instead of epsilon**c1, avoiding singularity at zero strain
- Arrhenius temperature dependence in deformation → exp(c0/T) or exp(-c0*T) factors reflecting thermally activated processes
- Concave-up vs concave-down stress-strain curves → Power exponent >1 (concave up) vs <1 (concave down/hardening saturation)
